<div id="review_3320987303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3320987303" />
    <a title="David Putnam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5463364-david-putnam"><img alt="David Putnam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372638034p2/5463364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3320987303?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Putnam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Putnam" href="/user/show/5463364-david-putnam">David Putnam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3320987303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14033420962467787818">Loved this book, it's a four point five and would've been a full five except for the ending. <br/>For me, great scifi is when the author doesn't start out telling me how this new world works. I'm far more interested in how the characters act/behave/ survive in this world that is unfamiliar to me. Good scifi hits the ground running giving the reader enough credit to keep up as the author slowly metes out the world building while setting a very dynamic conflict.<br/>My favorite scifi of late is Old Man's Wa</span>
  <span id="freeText14033420962467787818" style="display:none">Loved this book, it's a four point five and would've been a full five except for the ending. <br />For me, great scifi is when the author doesn't start out telling me how this new world works. I'm far more interested in how the characters act/behave/ survive in this world that is unfamiliar to me. Good scifi hits the ground running giving the reader enough credit to keep up as the author slowly metes out the world building while setting a very dynamic conflict.<br />My favorite scifi of late is Old Man's War, what a great read (along with the two followups). All systems Red is on this same level for me. The story starts off at a run and doesn't let up until the end. I loved it. <br />The minor problem for me is that in normal story arcs there are four sections, conflict, complication, crisis, and conclusion. This book has the crisis and the conclusion it runs so hot at such a frenetic pace the whole book feels like the crisis in the arc. Because of this the final crisis fizzles or pales to some of the wonderful earlier action scenes. This also happened for me in the book, Passages. The scene on train in that book made the ending feel like a fizzle. But oh, was that train scene something else.<br />Doesn't matter though, I picked all the other Martha Wells books. She can really write a strong female character that is viewed through the eyes of a murderbot.<br />David Putnam author of the Bruno Johnson series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14033420962467787818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2669018680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2669018680" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2669018680?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Robin by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/210123-d-g">D.G.</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2020">bb-b-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=audio-challenge-2020">audio-challenge-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=beautifully-broken-bastards">beautifully-broken-bastards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=no-kissy-kissy">no-kissy-kissy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2669018680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11234781841957496081"><b>Rereading Just in Time for the Next Book in this Series.</b><br/><br/>Just as much fun the second time around. Short, action packed and just enough of a story to make you fall for a Murderbot.<br/><br/><b>Original Review</b><br/><br/>I totally enjoyed this. As a book recommended to me by multiple good reads friends I knew that there was a high probability that would happen but what I didn’t expect was to fall in love with a SecUnit (<i>fancy talk for cyborg</i>) with a malfunctioning governors unit (<i>more fancy talk for something that makes yo</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11234781841957496081" style="display:none"><b>Rereading Just in Time for the Next Book in this Series.</b><br /><br />Just as much fun the second time around. Short, action packed and just enough of a story to make you fall for a Murderbot.<br /><br /><b>Original Review</b><br /><br />I totally enjoyed this. As a book recommended to me by multiple good reads friends I knew that there was a high probability that would happen but what I didn’t expect was to fall in love with a SecUnit (<i>fancy talk for cyborg</i>) with a malfunctioning governors unit (<i>more fancy talk for something that makes you behave</i>). <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I could have become a mass murderer after I hacked my governor module, but then I realized I could access the combined feed of entertainment channels carried on the company satellites. It had been well over 35,000 hours or so since then, with still not much murdering, but probably, I don't know, a little under 35,000 hours of movies, serials, books, plays, and music consumed. <b>As a heartless killing machine, I was a terrible failure.”</b></i>
</blockquote><br />Murderbot is assigned to a group of humans exploring a planet to see if it can be terraformed for a new colony. It is basically doing the least amount of work possible, just half-assing everything more worried about the serials it is watching that doing its job. Really it is just going through the motions for most things until everything starts going wrong for the team it is protecting and now Murderbot has to step up their game or all of the humans will end up dead and it will end up reprogrammed or worse.<br /><br />The humans in the party notice that something is maybe a little off about Murderbot just after one of its members is almost eaten by a huge wormish thing and all the trouble starts. Murderbot doesn’t enjoy one on one interaction with the team at all and it is hilarious some of the stuff it thinks while trying to learn how to by an integral member of the team and keep them alive.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Yes, talk to Murderbot about its feelings. The idea was so painful I dropped to 97 percent efficiency. I’d rather climb back into Hostile One’s mouth.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />The story is short but completely entertaining. It is what I always hope I’ll find in a SciFi book but rarely do. A fun story with a great cast of characters that doesn’t get too caught up on the geekiness factor and try to overexplain everything. This was just a great ride with a funny, pessimistic cyborg that has problems dealing with real people and prefers to hide behind an opaqued mask. I can totally relate to most of that anyway. But Murderbot is completely endearing in their own way.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Gurathin turned to me. "So you don't have a governor module, but we could punish you by looking at you."<br />I looked at him. "Probably, right up until I remember I have guns built into my arms.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />I’m completely hooked and will definitely catch up on the series as this seems like it is going to be a great ride.<br /><br />D.G. was the first friend to recommend this to me but not the last so thanks for the great recommendation guys.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11234781841957496081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2051975898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8642268007731565391">3ish stars.<br/><br/>Some heavy themes wrapped up in what is otherwise a relatively fluffy novella. The plot's straight-forward, the prose is decent, and it's charming and witty. Murderbot, who repeatedly says that she'd rather be netflixing, is surprisingly relatable. One of my favorite parts is when Murderbot is faced with the prospect of <i>spending time with people</i> and is (understandably) horrified. She can't control her facial reaction which in turn makes the human crew she's assigned to uncomfortable t</span>
  <span id="freeText8642268007731565391" style="display:none">3ish stars.<br /><br />Some heavy themes wrapped up in what is otherwise a relatively fluffy novella. The plot's straight-forward, the prose is decent, and it's charming and witty. Murderbot, who repeatedly says that she'd rather be netflixing, is surprisingly relatable. One of my favorite parts is when Murderbot is faced with the prospect of <i>spending time with people</i> and is (understandably) horrified. She can't control her facial reaction which in turn makes the human crew she's assigned to uncomfortable to know that they're making Murderbot uncomfortable (and that she has feelings as human as any of them). <br /><br />Also, I've just realized that I've been using female pronouns for Murderbot, when Murderbot is actually genderless and is referred to as 'it' by the crew. For some reason I naturally thought of Murderbot as being female and I'm not sure why, maybe because the author is a woman?<br /><br /><a href="https://mrphilipslibrary.wordpress.com/2017/10/09/all-systems-red-the-murderbot-diaries-1-by-martha-wells/" rel="nofollow noopener">Posted in Mr. Philip's Library</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8642268007731565391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2018">year-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372653123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4857250629074870978">The <i>Murderbot</i> novella series had crossed my path a time or two before I finally picked it up, but it was the glowing recommendation from my book buddy TS & the convenient timing of an Audible Daily Deal that pushed my curiosity over the edge! <br/><br/>This was such an adorable story, which is ironic since the name of the series is <i>Murderbot.</i> But despite Murderbot's name for itself, it's actually a rather hilarious & relatable individual. <br/><br/>Being deeply invested in downloaded media & characterized by it's i</span>
  <span id="freeText4857250629074870978" style="display:none">The <i>Murderbot</i> novella series had crossed my path a time or two before I finally picked it up, but it was the glowing recommendation from my book buddy TS &amp; the convenient timing of an Audible Daily Deal that pushed my curiosity over the edge! <br /><br />This was such an adorable story, which is ironic since the name of the series is <i>Murderbot.</i> But despite Murderbot's name for itself, it's actually a rather hilarious &amp; relatable individual. <br /><br />Being deeply invested in downloaded media &amp; characterized by it's inability to interact with humans without being awkward, I feel as though Murderbot will connect with many readers on a personal level.<br /><br />The short arc of this story is entertaining to say the least &amp; even manages to pack in some heavy themes about autonomy &amp; friendship (HELLO THIS IS WHAT I WANTED BUT DID NOT GET FROM AUTONOMOUS!) <br /><br />It really appeals to my desire for Science Fiction that doesn't require hundreds of pages &amp; convoluted paragraphs to make its point. I'll definitely be continuing on, as I'm intrigued to see what more is in store for Murderbot! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4857250629074870978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Consider me glued.</span>

<div id="review_1981748167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981748167" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1981748167?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/37432805-all-systems-red">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981748167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10776799363700383763">This is a novella nominated for several awards and I know why. <br/><br/>In this story, a security robot breaks its own company protocol, freeing itself from any restraints, thus allowing its personality to unfold. Through the eyes of "Murderbot" (she's named herself that way), we experience what it is like to work with and for humans, that humans come in all forms (good and bad and everything in between), what the company creating these robots programs them to do (and what not) - and, ultimately, we lear</span>
  <span id="freeText10776799363700383763" style="display:none">This is a novella nominated for several awards and I know why. <br /><br />In this story, a security robot breaks its own company protocol, freeing itself from any restraints, thus allowing its personality to unfold. Through the eyes of "Murderbot" (she's named herself that way), we experience what it is like to work with and for humans, that humans come in all forms (good and bad and everything in between), what the company creating these robots programs them to do (and what not) - and, ultimately, we learn how confusing and difficult it is to find oneself.<br /><br />Murderbot doesn't like humans very much. But it isn't hatred - rather, confusion. Add to that that she is SHY! Yep, a security bot made to kill people (and other stuff) is actually shy and would rather watch TV. *lol*<br /><br />The writing was fast-paced and engaging, every character lively and distinct (not always easy, especially not in short stories) and the unobtrusive humour was delightful.<br /><br />I will definitely continue reading this series after the great ending to this and can't wait to know more about Murderbot's adventures and self-discovery that also teach us a lot about what it is to be "human".</span>
  <a data-text-id="10776799363700383763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1932908963" />
    <a title="Mir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/237469-mir"><img alt="Mir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275489063p2/237469.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1932908963?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mir" href="/user/show/237469-mir">Mir</a>
      </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('568d2kJVwlXRyRlky6T3k4wshHiINkZzbh2GdFp4e+bA2kfy6BUEISj2SI76Bhxstg5lIc+cyKEechQOs4oUJw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ooKg3U8m9x4O5r4c1GaR0zHLthAF1CNz1qCR0qc+42GF9/r15WYxavfZ7/blxHosC+lXSUJ+raGmzwOoTsyMoA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12410729897344351255"> Martha Wells has written many fantasy novels, including The Books of the Raksura series (beginning with <i>The Cloud Roads</i>), the Ile-Rien series (including <i>The Death of the Necromancer</i>) as well as YA fantasy novels, short stories, media tie-ins (for <i>Star Wars</i> and <i>Stargate: Atlantis</i>), and non-fiction. Her most recent fantasy novel is <i>The Harbors of the Sun</i> in 2017, the final novel in The Books of the</span>
  <span id="freeText12410729897344351255" style="display:none"> Martha Wells has written many fantasy novels, including The Books of the Raksura series (beginning with <i>The Cloud Roads</i>), the Ile-Rien series (including <i>The Death of the Necromancer</i>) as well as YA fantasy novels, short stories, media tie-ins (for <i>Star Wars</i> and <i>Stargate: Atlantis</i>), and non-fiction. Her most recent fantasy novel is <i>The Harbors of the Sun</i> in 2017, the final novel in The Books of the Raksura series. She has a new series of SF novellas, <i>The Murderbot Diaries</i>, published by Tor.com in 2017 and 2018. She was also the lead writer for the story team of <i>Magic: the Gathering</i>'s Dominaria expansion in 2018. She has won a Nebula Award, two Hugo Awards, an ALA/YALSA Alex Award, a Locus Award, and her work has appeared on the Philip K. Dick Award ballot, the USA Today Bestseller List, and the New York Times Bestseller List. Her books have been published in eleven languages. <br /><br />She has had short stories in the magazines <i>Black Gate</i>, <i>Realms of Fantasy</i>, <i>Lone Star Stories</i>, <i>Lightspeed Magazine</i>, and <i>Stargate Magazine</i>, and in the Tsunami Relief anthology <i>Elemental</i>, <i>The Other Half of the Sky</i>, <i>Tales of the Emerald Serpent</i>, <i>Mech: Age of Steel</i>, and <i>The Gods of Lovecraft</i>. <br /><br />She has essays in the nonfiction anthologies <i>Farscape Forever</i>, <i>Mapping the World of Harry Potter</i>, <i>Chicks Unravel Time</i>, and <i>The Kobold Guide to Magic</i>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12410729897344351255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
